     112             : 
     113             : /*
     114             :  * Create a trigger.  Returns the address of the created trigger.
     115             :  *
     116             :  * queryString is the source text of the CREATE TRIGGER command.
     117             :  * This must be supplied if a whenClause is specified, else it can be NULL.
     118             :  *
     119             :  * relOid, if nonzero, is the relation on which the trigger should be
     120             :  * created.  If zero, the name provided in the statement will be looked up.
     121             :  *
     122             :  * refRelOid, if nonzero, is the relation to which the constraint trigger
     123             :  * refers.  If zero, the constraint relation name provided in the statement
     124             :  * will be looked up as needed.
     125             :  *
     126             :  * constraintOid, if nonzero, says that this trigger is being created
     127             :  * internally to implement that constraint.  A suitable pg_depend entry will
     128             :  * be made to link the trigger to that constraint.  constraintOid is zero when
     129             :  * executing a user-entered CREATE TRIGGER command.  (For CREATE CONSTRAINT
     130             :  * TRIGGER, we build a pg_constraint entry internally.)
     131             :  *
     132             :  * indexOid, if nonzero, is the OID of an index associated with the constraint.
     133             :  * We do nothing with this except store it into pg_trigger.tgconstrindid;
     134             :  * but when creating a trigger for a deferrable unique constraint on a
     135             :  * partitioned table, its children are looked up.  Note we don't cope with
     136             :  * invalid indexes in that case.
     137             :  *
     138             :  * funcoid, if nonzero, is the OID of the function to invoke.  When this is
     139             :  * given, stmt->funcname is ignored.
     140             :  *
     141             :  * parentTriggerOid, if nonzero, is a trigger that begets this one; so that
     142             :  * if that trigger is dropped, this one should be too.  There are two cases
     143             :  * when a nonzero value is passed for this: 1) when this function recurses to
     144             :  * create the trigger on partitions, 2) when creating child foreign key
     145             :  * triggers; see CreateFKCheckTrigger() and createForeignKeyActionTriggers().
     146             :  *
     147             :  * If whenClause is passed, it is an already-transformed expression for
     148             :  * WHEN.  In this case, we ignore any that may come in stmt->whenClause.
     149             :  *
     150             :  * If isInternal is true then this is an internally-generated trigger.
     151             :  * This argument sets the tgisinternal field of the pg_trigger entry, and
     152             :  * if true causes us to modify the given trigger name to ensure uniqueness.
     153             :  *
     154             :  * When isInternal is not true we require ACL_TRIGGER permissions on the
     155             :  * relation, as well as ACL_EXECUTE on the trigger function.  For internal
     156             :  * triggers the caller must apply any required permission checks.
     157             :  *
     158             :  * When called on partitioned tables, this function recurses to create the
     159             :  * trigger on all the partitions, except if isInternal is true, in which
     160             :  * case caller is expected to execute recursion on its own.  in_partition
     161             :  * indicates such a recursive call; outside callers should pass "false"
     162             :  * (but see CloneRowTriggersToPartition).
     163             :  */
     164             : ObjectAddress

    3528             : /* ----------

    3531             :  * The AfterTriggersData struct holds data about pending AFTER trigger events

    3533             :  * immediately so we don't need any persistent state about them.)  The struct
    3534             :  * and most of its subsidiary data are kept in TopTransactionContext; however
    3535             :  * some data that can be discarded sooner appears in the CurTransactionContext
    3536             :  * of the relevant subtransaction.  Also, the individual event records are
    3537             :  * kept in a separate sub-context of TopTransactionContext.  This is done
    3538             :  * mainly so that it's easy to tell from a memory context dump how much space
    3539             :  * is being eaten by trigger events.
    3540             :  *
    3541             :  * Because the list of pending events can grow large, we go to some
    3542             :  * considerable effort to minimize per-event memory consumption.  The event
    3543             :  * records are grouped into chunks and common data for similar events in the
    3544             :  * same chunk is only stored once.

    3546             :  * XXX We need to be able to save the per-event data in a file if it grows too

    3582             : /*
    3583             :  * Per-trigger-event data
    3584             :  *
    3585             :  * The actual per-event data, AfterTriggerEventData, includes DONE/IN_PROGRESS
    3586             :  * status bits, up to two tuple CTIDs, and optionally two OIDs of partitions.
    3587             :  * Each event record also has an associated AfterTriggerSharedData that is
    3588             :  * shared across all instances of similar events within a "chunk".
    3589             :  *
    3590             :  * For row-level triggers, we arrange not to waste storage on unneeded ctid
    3591             :  * fields.  Updates of regular tables use two; inserts and deletes of regular
    3592             :  * tables use one; foreign tables always use zero and save the tuple(s) to a
    3593             :  * tuplestore.  AFTER_TRIGGER_FDW_FETCH directs AfterTriggerExecute() to
    3594             :  * retrieve a fresh tuple or pair of tuples from that tuplestore, while
    3595             :  * AFTER_TRIGGER_FDW_REUSE directs it to use the most-recently-retrieved
    3596             :  * tuple(s).  This permits storing tuples once regardless of the number of
    3597             :  * row-level triggers on a foreign table.
    3598             :  *
    3599             :  * When updates on partitioned tables cause rows to move between partitions,
    3600             :  * the OIDs of both partitions are stored too, so that the tuples can be
    3601             :  * fetched; such entries are marked AFTER_TRIGGER_CP_UPDATE (for "cross-
    3602             :  * partition update").
    3603             :  *
    3604             :  * Note that we need triggers on foreign tables to be fired in exactly the
    3605             :  * order they were queued, so that the tuples come out of the tuplestore in
    3606             :  * the right order.  To ensure that, we forbid deferrable (constraint)
    3607             :  * triggers on foreign tables.  This also ensures that such triggers do not
    3608             :  * get deferred into outer trigger query levels, meaning that it's okay to
    3609             :  * destroy the tuplestore at the end of the query level.
    3610             :  *
    3611             :  * Statement-level triggers always bear AFTER_TRIGGER_1CTID, though they
    3612             :  * require no ctid field.  We lack the flag bit space to neatly represent that
    3613             :  * distinct case, and it seems unlikely to be worth much trouble.
    3614             :  *
    3615             :  * Note: ats_firing_id is initially zero and is set to something else when
    3616             :  * AFTER_TRIGGER_IN_PROGRESS is set.  It indicates which trigger firing
    3617             :  * cycle the trigger will be fired in (or was fired in, if DONE is set).
    3618             :  * Although this is mutable state, we can keep it in AfterTriggerSharedData
    3619             :  * because all instances of the same type of event in a given event list will
    3620             :  * be fired at the same time, if they were queued between the same firing
    3621             :  * cycles.  So we need only ensure that ats_firing_id is zero when attaching
    3622             :  * a new event to an existing AfterTriggerSharedData record.

    3744             : /*
    3745             :  * All per-transaction data for the AFTER TRIGGERS module.
    3746             :  *
    3747             :  * AfterTriggersData has the following fields:
    3748             :  *
    3749             :  * firing_counter is incremented for each call of afterTriggerInvokeEvents.
    3750             :  * We mark firable events with the current firing cycle's ID so that we can
    3751             :  * tell which ones to work on.  This ensures sane behavior if a trigger
    3752             :  * function chooses to do SET CONSTRAINTS: the inner SET CONSTRAINTS will
    3753             :  * only fire those events that weren't already scheduled for firing.
    3754             :  *
    3755             :  * state keeps track of the transaction-local effects of SET CONSTRAINTS.
    3756             :  * This is saved and restored across failed subtransactions.
    3757             :  *
    3758             :  * events is the current list of deferred events.  This is global across
    3759             :  * all subtransactions of the current transaction.  In a subtransaction
    3760             :  * abort, we know that the events added by the subtransaction are at the
    3761             :  * end of the list, so it is relatively easy to discard them.  The event
    3762             :  * list chunks themselves are stored in event_cxt.
    3763             :  *
    3764             :  * query_depth is the current depth of nested AfterTriggerBeginQuery calls
    3765             :  * (-1 when the stack is empty).
    3766             :  *
    3767             :  * query_stack[query_depth] is the per-query-level data, including these fields:
    3768             :  *
    3769             :  * events is a list of AFTER trigger events queued by the current query.
    3770             :  * None of these are valid until the matching AfterTriggerEndQuery call
    3771             :  * occurs.  At that point we fire immediate-mode triggers, and append any
    3772             :  * deferred events to the main events list.
    3773             :  *
    3774             :  * fdw_tuplestore is a tuplestore containing the foreign-table tuples
    3775             :  * needed by events queued by the current query.  (Note: we use just one
    3776             :  * tuplestore even though more than one foreign table might be involved.
    3777             :  * This is okay because tuplestores don't really care what's in the tuples
    3778             :  * they store; but it's possible that someday it'd break.)
    3779             :  *
    3780             :  * tables is a List of AfterTriggersTableData structs for target tables
    3781             :  * of the current query (see below).
    3782             :  *
    3783             :  * maxquerydepth is just the allocated length of query_stack.
    3784             :  *
    3785             :  * trans_stack holds per-subtransaction data, including these fields:
    3786             :  *
    3787             :  * state is NULL or a pointer to a saved copy of the SET CONSTRAINTS
    3788             :  * state data.  Each subtransaction level that modifies that state first
    3789             :  * saves a copy, which we use to restore the state if we abort.
    3790             :  *
    3791             :  * events is a copy of the events head/tail pointers,
    3792             :  * which we use to restore those values during subtransaction abort.
    3793             :  *
    3794             :  * query_depth is the subtransaction-start-time value of query_depth,
    3795             :  * which we similarly use to clean up at subtransaction abort.
    3796             :  *
    3797             :  * firing_counter is the subtransaction-start-time value of firing_counter.
    3798             :  * We use this to recognize which deferred triggers were fired (or marked
    3799             :  * for firing) within an aborted subtransaction.
    3800             :  *
    3801             :  * We use GetCurrentTransactionNestLevel() to determine the correct array
    3802             :  * index in trans_stack.  maxtransdepth is the number of allocated entries in
    3803             :  * trans_stack.  (By not keeping our own stack pointer, we can avoid trouble
    3804             :  * in cases where errors during subxact abort cause multiple invocations
    3805             :  * of AfterTriggerEndSubXact() at the same nesting depth.)
    3806             :  *
    3807             :  * We create an AfterTriggersTableData struct for each target table of the
    3808             :  * current query, and each operation mode (INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE), that has
    3809             :  * either transition tables or statement-level triggers.  This is used to
    3810             :  * hold the relevant transition tables, as well as info tracking whether
    3811             :  * we already queued the statement triggers.  (We use that info to prevent
    3812             :  * firing the same statement triggers more than once per statement, or really
    3813             :  * once per transition table set.)  These structs, along with the transition
    3814             :  * table tuplestores, live in the (sub)transaction's CurTransactionContext.
    3815             :  * That's sufficient lifespan because we don't allow transition tables to be
    3816             :  * used by deferrable triggers, so they only need to survive until
    3817             :  * AfterTriggerEndQuery.
    3818             :  */
    3819             : typedef struct AfterTriggersQueryData AfterTriggersQueryData;

    4868             :  * to decide whether to capture tuples in transition tables.
    4869             :  *

    4874             :  * dealing with child tables, the caller can set tcs_original_insert_tuple

    4881             :  *
    4882             :  * Per SQL spec, all operations of the same kind (INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE)
    4883             :  * on the same table during one query should share one transition table.
    4884             :  * Therefore, the Tuplestores are owned by an AfterTriggersTableData struct
    4885             :  * looked up using the table OID + CmdType, and are merely referenced by

    6026             : /* ----------
    6027             :  * AfterTriggerSaveEvent()
    6028             :  *
    6029             :  *  Called by ExecA[RS]...Triggers() to queue up the triggers that should
    6030             :  *  be fired for an event.
    6031             :  *
    6032             :  *  NOTE: this is called whenever there are any triggers associated with
    6033             :  *  the event (even if they are disabled).  This function decides which
    6034             :  *  triggers actually need to be queued.  It is also called after each row,
    6035             :  *  even if there are no triggers for that event, if there are any AFTER
    6036             :  *  STATEMENT triggers for the statement which use transition tables, so that
    6037             :  *  the transition tuplestores can be built.  Furthermore, if the transition
    6038             :  *  capture is happening for UPDATEd rows being moved to another partition due
    6039             :  *  to the partition-key being changed, then this function is called once when
    6040             :  *  the row is deleted (to capture OLD row), and once when the row is inserted
    6041             :  *  into another partition (to capture NEW row).  This is done separately because
    6042             :  *  DELETE and INSERT happen on different tables.
    6043             :  *
    6044             :  *  Transition tuplestores are built now, rather than when events are pulled
    6045             :  *  off of the queue because AFTER ROW triggers are allowed to select from the
    6046             :  *  transition tables for the statement.
    6047             :  *
    6048             :  *  This contains special support to queue the update events for the case where
    6049             :  *  a partitioned table undergoing a cross-partition update may have foreign
    6050             :  *  keys pointing into it.  Normally, a partitioned table's row triggers are
    6051             :  *  not fired because the leaf partition(s) which are modified as a result of
    6052             :  *  the operation on the partitioned table contain the same triggers which are
    6053             :  *  fired instead. But that general scheme can cause problematic behavior with
    6054             :  *  foreign key triggers during cross-partition updates, which are implemented
    6055             :  *  as DELETE on the source partition followed by INSERT into the destination
    6056             :  *  partition.  Specifically, firing DELETE triggers would lead to the wrong
    6057             :  *  foreign key action to be enforced considering that the original command is
    6058             :  *  UPDATE; in this case, this function is called with relinfo as the
    6059             :  *  partitioned table, and src_partinfo and dst_partinfo referring to the
    6060             :  *  source and target leaf partitions, respectively.
    6061             :  *
    6062             :  *  is_crosspart_update is true either when a DELETE event is fired on the
    6063             :  *  source partition (which is to be ignored) or an UPDATE event is fired on
    6064             :  *  the root partitioned table.
    6065             :  * ----------
    6066             :  */
